.. index:: pair: typedef; shm_buffer_draw_t

	typedef void (*shm_buffer_draw_t)(
		struct tw_appsurf *surf,

one of the implementation of :ref:`tw_appsurf <doxid-d6/d55/structtw__appsurf>`

.. index:: pair: function; thread_run_module
.. _doxid-d4/dde/console__module_8c_1ad5bd64764e31fe7c330d4b38560de8d3:

.. ref-code-block:: cpp
	:class: doxyrest-title-code-block

	void* thread_run_module(void* arg)

running thread for the module,

module thread is a consumer for commands and producer for results. If the results is not taken, it needs to clean up before do it again.

Console thread does the reverse. It is the consumer of results and producer of commands, if the commands it produced is not taken, it needs to reset it manually.

We have a general cache method to reduce the uncessary module searching.

.. index:: pair: function; conversation
.. _doxid-d9/de2/shell__lock_8c_1aefcbb7b234b45b9a074200cdb4e4024e:

.. ref-code-block:: cpp
	:class: doxyrest-title-code-block

	static int conversation(
		int num_msg,
		const struct pam_message** msgs,
		struct pam_response** resp,
		void* appdata_ptr
		)

This function performs a conversation between our application and and the module. It receives an array of messages in the parameters (set by the module) and sets the array of responses in the parameters with the appropriate content. For example if the module calls this function with a message "login:" we are expected to set the firs response with the username.



.. rubric:: Parameters:

.. list-table::
	:widths: 20 80

	*
		- num_msg

		- Number of messages from the module

	*
		- msg

		- Array of messages (set by the module, should not be modified)

	*
		- resp

		- Array of responses this function must set

	*
		- appdata_ptr

		- Pointer to additional data. The pointer received is that specified in the pam_conv structure below.

add_key_bindings

going through the tree structure to add leaves. We are taking the considerration of collisions, this is IMPORTANT because we can only activate one grab at a time.

If there are collisions, the keybinding is not not added to the system.

.. index:: pair: function; tdbus_readv
.. _doxid-d2/d1b/tdbus_8h_1adace5ed8eb2b885937dfad2678797641:

.. ref-code-block:: cpp
	:class: doxyrest-title-code-block

	void tdbus_readv(
		const struct :ref:`tdbus_message<doxid-d9/db6/structtdbus__message>`* msg,
		const char* format,
		va_list ap
		)

reading a message

if you are a client, most likeyly you are reading a signal or a method reply. Given you call them correctly. If you know the argument of message you expect, call directly tdbus_read(v). Use tdbus_read(v) inside @tdbus_read_signal_f or @tdbus_read_reply_f. You can verify the signature of the incoming message with your reader to determine would that be what you expect.

If you are a server, you may expect clients are calling your methods, implement @tdbus_read_call_f for that.

Currently @tdbus_readv and @tdbus_writev only supports basic types.

.. index:: pair: function; tdbus_writev

.. index:: pair: function; tw_event_get_udev_device

		struct :ref:`tw_event_queue<doxid-d3/d59/structtw__event__queue>`* queue,

		)

returns an allocated udev_device

you have the responsibility to free the allocated ``udev_device`` by calling ``udev_device_unref``. And you should only call this function with udev event, otherwise the behavior is undefined

.. index:: pair: function; tw_event_queue_add_idle
.. _doxid-d2/d4f/event__queue_8h_1a265f0f9f49954e7c7d15c9abb64ef8e6:

.. ref-code-block:: cpp
	:class: doxyrest-title-code-block

	bool tw_event_queue_add_idle(struct :ref:`tw_event_queue<doxid-d3/d59/structtw__event__queue>`* queue, struct :ref:`tw_event<doxid-db/dc2/structtw__event>`* e)

add the idle task to the queue.

You could have a lot of allocation under one frame. So use this feature carefully. For example, use a cached state to check whether it is necessary to add to this list.

an example of event would be resize event, this event is delegated from a wl_event.

.. index:: pair: function; tw_appsurf_request_frame

	void tw_appsurf_request_frame(struct :ref:`tw_appsurf<doxid-d6/d55/structtw__appsurf>`* surf)

request a frame for the appsurface

You can use this callback to start the animation sequence for the surface, so frame the next draw call, the app will be in animation. You can stop the animation by calling ``tw_appsurf_end_frame_request``. The function is intentioned to be used directly in the ``frame_callback`` kick start the animation.

.. index:: pair: function; shm_wl_buffer_release
.. _doxid-da/d05/appsurf_8c_1adce0812a181cbd470a0ce135433510b4:

.. ref-code-block:: cpp
	:class: doxyrest-title-code-block

	static void shm_wl_buffer_release(void* data, struct wl_buffer* wl_buffer)

smartly release the buffer and pool.

We are waiting for compositor to return all the buffers. There could be cases where we switched to new pool before compositor returns the buffers from previous pool. In that case the previous pool becomes a wild pointer. The pool will eventually be freed here if ``compositor`` finally returns the buffer back to us.

.. _doxid-d0/d26/event__queue_8c_1a25b1f33de9ac79559777d956dbf7284d:

.. ref-code-block:: cpp
	:class: doxyrest-title-code-block

	WL_EXPORT struct udev_device* tw_event_get_udev_device(
		struct :ref:`tw_event_queue<doxid-d3/d59/structtw__event__queue>`* queue,
		int fd
		)

returns an allocated udev_device

you have the responsibility to free the allocated ``udev_device`` by calling ``udev_device_unref``. And you should only call this function with udev event, otherwise the behavior is undefined

.. index:: pair: function; tw_event_queue_add_idle
.. _doxid-d0/d26/event__queue_8c_1ae3398df716504fac1f726524ef181f39:

.. ref-code-block:: cpp
	:class: doxyrest-title-code-block

	WL_EXPORT bool tw_event_queue_add_idle(
		struct :ref:`tw_event_queue<doxid-d3/d59/structtw__event__queue>`* queue,
		struct :ref:`tw_event<doxid-db/dc2/structtw__event>`* event
		)

add the idle task to the queue.

You could have a lot of allocation under one frame. So use this feature carefully. For example, use a cached state to check whether it is necessary to add to this list.

an example of event would be resize event, this event is delegated from a wl_event.

.. index:: pair: function; tw_mat3_wl_transform
.. _doxid-dd/df4/matrix_8h_1a72312e0d4794589d6b3c4f8135b6497a:

.. ref-code-block:: cpp
	:class: doxyrest-title-code-block

	void tw_mat3_wl_transform(
		struct :ref:`tw_mat3<doxid-d4/da4/structtw__mat3>`* dst,
		enum wl_output_transform transform,
		bool yup
		)

rotate by wl_transform



.. rubric:: Parameters:

.. list-table::
	:widths: 20 80

	*
		- yup

		- is true for x-right, y-up coordinates system, OpenGL uses this system, where bottom-left is the origin. yup is false for x-right, y-down coordinates system, wayland coordinates system uses this coordinates, where top-left is the origin.

.. index:: pair: function; tw_mat3_transform_rect
.. _doxid-dd/df4/matrix_8h_1a3d99f657460fcee357285c2d5589693d:

.. ref-code-block:: cpp
	:class: doxyrest-title-code-block

	void tw_mat3_transform_rect(
		struct :ref:`tw_mat3<doxid-d4/da4/structtw__mat3>`* dst,
		bool yup,
		enum wl_output_transform transform,
		uint32_t width,
		uint32_t height,
		uint32_t scale
		)

@breif transform a (0, 0, width, height) by its size

the (width, height) here is needed to move the rect back to origin after multiplied by rotation and scaling matrix

.. index:: pair: function; tw_mat3_ortho_proj
.. _doxid-dd/df4/matrix_8h_1ae14cfd25f84fdb1f944c3a34b25222ac:

.. ref-code-block:: cpp
	:class: doxyrest-title-code-block

	void tw_mat3_ortho_proj(struct :ref:`tw_mat3<doxid-d4/da4/structtw__mat3>`* dst, uint32_t width, uint32_t height)

generating matrix mapping coordinates from image space to clip space.

The mapping procedure goes as following:

(0, 0, width, height) --> (-1, -1, 1, 1) xp = 2\*x/width - 1.0 yp = 2\*y/height - 1.0

We take the image space coordiantes(in the wl_transformed output), which the origin is the top-left cornor. We need to map them into clip space, which the origin is the center of monitor. Then we apply the inverse wl_transform of the output to get actual device coordinates.

NDC_coord = wl_transform \* proj \* image_coord

Additional transformation can happen between projection and wl_transform, for example an additional scaling can be applyed.



.. rubric:: Parameters:

.. list-table::
	:widths: 20 80

	*
		- width

		- is the width of the transformed output.

	*
		- height

		- is the height pf the transformed output.

.. index:: pair: function; tw_launch_client
.. _doxid-d2/dd7/subprocess_8h_1a22865274dc2adc4db436bdf79fed06d5:

.. ref-code-block:: cpp
	:class: doxyrest-title-code-block

	struct wl_client* tw_launch_client(
		struct wl_display* display,
		const char* path,
		struct :ref:`tw_subprocess<doxid-d0/d68/structtw__subprocess>`* chld
		)

front end of tw_launch_client_complex

works like tw_launch_client_complex(ec, path, chld, NULL, NULL);

.. index:: pair: function; tw_launch_client_complex
.. _doxid-d2/dd7/subprocess_8h_1a575dea2a5a3a0d11cd56d1f3921c0c9a:

.. ref-code-block:: cpp
	:class: doxyrest-title-code-block

	struct wl_client* tw_launch_client_complex(
		struct wl_display* display,
		const char* path,
		struct :ref:`tw_subprocess<doxid-d0/d68/structtw__subprocess>`* chld,
		int(*)(pid_t, struct :ref:`tw_subprocess<doxid-d0/d68/structtw__subprocess>`*) fork,
		int(*)(const char*, struct :ref:`tw_subprocess<doxid-d0/d68/structtw__subprocess>`*) exec
		)

launch wayland client

this function follows the fork-exec routine and creates a new wayland client, setting wayland socket is taking care of and you can optionally set your own fork and exec routine.

The optional fork routine is done after fork() is called. It can be used to setup the post forking procedures for parent and child process.

The optional exec routine need to actually call exec\*() and return the non-zero if it fails.
